Nos. 127  &amp; 129/09)</span></b><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span  style='font-size:8.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:  "Courier New"'>) </span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><b  style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:8.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:  11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span  style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Prosenjit Kumar Shaha and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">. . . </span></strong><!-- [if supportFields]><b  style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:  110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><span  style='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(Respondents,</span></b><b  style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:  11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>(In both appeals)</span></b><b  style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:  110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>) </span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><b  style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:  110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: left;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Transfer of Property Act (IV of 1882)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="color: #000000;">Section 123</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">‘<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Youtuka’</em> is a kind of gift and such gift if made at the time of marriage of daughter is valid in respect of immovable property and no registration is required according to section 123 of the Transfer of Property Act.<span style="mso-tab-count: 2;">               </span>. . . (17)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Transfer of Property Act (IV of 1882)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Section 122</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">This term “Youtuka” has been interpreted by the High Court Division of Calcutta as including not only gifts made before the nuptial fire but gifts made during continuance of the marriage ceremonies, that is, the ceremonies beginning with shraddha and ending with that of <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">prostrating before the husband. It is </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">conceived</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;"> that it includes gifts from strangers</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">made before the nuptial fire and at the bridal</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">procession. <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘Youtuka’</em>, that is, gift </span></span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.5pt;">of immovable</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.4pt;"> property made as consideration</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> of marriage at the time of nuptial fire is valid.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>. . . (17 and 20)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Transfer of Property Act (IV of 1882)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Section 123</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 9.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The appellate Court rightly found that Dharijyamoyee could legally transfer the property which she got in life interest to Panchanani for legal necessity. The appellate Court noted that Dharijyamoyee became blind and Panchanani used to look after her and that prompted Dharijyamoyee to make gift of half of ‘Kha’ schedule land to Panchanani. Thereafter, Panchanani validly acquired half of ‘Kha’ schedule land by the deed of gift dated 07.10.1941.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                          </span>. . (22)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 9.0pt; text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Prem Mohan Das Vs. Hari Mohan Das, ILR (1952) 52 Calcutta 426 ref. </span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 1.0in;"><!-- [if supportFields]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(For the Appellants,(</span></i></b><istyle='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><span style='font-size:10.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>In all the appeals</span></i><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><i style='mso-bidi-font-style:normal'><spanstyle='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>)) </span></i></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Shahidul Islam, Advocate, instructed by Mrs. Shirin Afroz,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Advocate-on-Record. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mr. Mojibur Rahman, Advocate-on-Record. </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; font-variant: small-caps;">Syed Mahmud Hossain, J</span></u></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; font-variant: small-caps;">:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">All the appeals by leave are directed against the common judgment and order dated 10.07.2008 passed by the High Court Division making the Rules absolute in Civil Revision Nos. 571, 572, 573 of 1987 and discharging the Rules in Civil Revision Nos. 8692, 9205 and 9106 of 1991.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">All the appeals involving similar questions</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> of laws and facts having been heard together are now disposed of by this single judgment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The facts, leading to the filing of these appeals, in a nutshell, are: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Prosenjit Kumar Saha and others as the plaintiffs filed Title Suit Nos.980, 982 and 983 of 1975 against Abdur Rahim Mollah and Rashik Lal Saha in the Third Court of the then<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Munsif, Pabna for declaration of title to the suit land. Subsequently, the suits were renumbered as Other Class Suit Nos.36, 37 and 38 of 1984. Their case, in short, is that the suit property described in ‘Ka’ schedule to the plaint originally belonged to Banomadhab Saha, while ‘Kha’ schedule land to Banomadhab Saha and one Jatish Chandra Saha in equal 8 annas share. Banomadhab Saha had no son but had a daughter Panchanani Saha. He orally gifted his entire property to his daughter Panchanani Saha as ‘Yautaka’, during her marriage with Sarart Chandra, who began to live in the house of Banomadhab as domesticated son-in-law and possessed the gifted property. Jotish Chandra Saha gifted his 8 annas share to his mother Dharijyamoyee Saha and delivered possession to her, who in course of her owning and possessing in her absolute right, gifted the same to her brother-in-law’s daughter Panchanani by a registered deed of gift dated 07.10.1941. Said Panchanani thereby became owner of 16 annas share of the entire suit property described in ‘Ka’ and ‘Kha’ schedules to the plaint. While owning and possessing the same through her bargadars, she died on 05.12.1967 childless but her husband Sarat Chandra while owning and possessing the same died on 16.03.1972 leaving behind 3 grand sons, namely, Prosanjit, Nitai and Amarendra, all son’s sons of Sarashibala, the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>predeceased first wife Banamadhab. The aforesaid grandsons of of Banamadhab are the plaintiffs in the instant suit and they became owners of 16 annas share of the suit property. Defendant No.1, Abul Hossain Khan, a desperate person, disclosed in the month of July,1976 that he has purchased the suit property in the month of Joistha,1383 B.S. from defendant No.2, Rashik Lal but as a matter of fact, he had no interest whatsoever in the property inasmuch as his father Tustalal, full sister’s son of Banomadhab had died before Panchanani on 30.03.1965 Thus the plaintiffs’ title became clouded and hence the suit was filed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Defendant No.1 contested the suit by filing written statement, denying all the material statements made in the plaint. His case, in short, is that Banomadhab and Banamali were 2 full brothers. The suit properties described in ‘Ka’ schedule to the plaint belonged to Banomadhab while ‘Kha’ schedule to Banamali in 8 annas shares. Jyotish Chandra son of Banomali died leaving his mother Dharijamoyee and full paternal uncle Banomadhab. Dharijiamoyee possessed 8 annas share in limited life interest and then died leaving behind aforesaid Banomadhab, who died leaving a barren daughter Panchanani and full sister’s son Tustalal, who inherited the property and began to possess the same through bargadars under the care of Panchanani and then died leaving a son Rashiklal, who sold the suit properties to defendant No.1 by kabala dated 11.06.1976. Defendant No.1 remained in possession thereon since then. The suits are liable to be dismissed with cost. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The trial Court by judgment and order dated 31.07.1985 dismissed all the suits. Against the said judgment and decrees of the trial Court, the plaintiffs preferred Other Class Appeal Nos.157, 158 and 159 of 1995 before the learned District Judge, Pabna, who by his judgment and order dated 26.11.1986 allowed the appeals in part and decreed the suit in respect of 8 annas share in ‘Kha’ schedule land in favour of the plaintiffs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Being aggrieved by the aforesaid judgment and decree passed by the appellate Court, the plaintiffs preferred three revisional applications before the High Court Division and obtained Rules in Civil Revision Nos.571, 572 and 573 of 1987 and defendant No.1 preferred three<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>revisional applications before the High Court Division and obtained Rules in Civil Revision Nos.8692, 9106 and 9206 of 1991. The learned Single Judge of the High Court Division, upon hearing the parties, by the judgment and order dated 10.07.2008 made the Rules absolute in Civil Revision Nos.571, 572 and 573 of 1987 and discharged the Rules in Civil Revision Nos.8692, 9106 and 9206 of 1991. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Feeling aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned judgment and order dated 10.07.2008 passed by the High Court Division, the leave-petitioners have filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal Nos.1936-1941 of 2008 and obtained leave in all the petitions on 12.04.2009 resulting in Civil Appeal Nos.325-330 of 2009. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Shahidul Islam, learned Advocate, appearing on behalf of the appellants in all the appeals, submits that the High Court Division failed to consider the evidence on record that the plaintiffs hopelessly failed to prove their title to and possession in the suit land. He lastly submits that the High Court Division failed to consider properly the meaning of gift under Hindu Law and the law relating to transfer of immovable property through gift. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Probir Neogi, learned Senior Advocate, appearing on behalf of the respondents in all the appeals, on the other hand, submits that the plaintiffs inherited ‘Ka’ schedule and half of ‘Kha’ schedule property, which is <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“Youtuka”</em> of Panchanani and they inherited half of ‘Kha’ schedule land as grandsons of Panchanani’s husband Sharat Chandra. He then submits that the defendant miserably failed to prove that Panchanani was a concubine of Sharat Chandra and that exhibit-3, the deed of gift of the year,1941 proves that she is in fact the wife of Sharat Chandra and as such, no interference is called for. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">We have considered the submissions of the learned Advocate for the appellants and the learned Senior Advocate for the respondents, perused the impugned judgment and the materials on record. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Before addressing the conflicting submissions of the learned Advocates of both the sides, it would be pertinent to go through the grounds, for which, leave was granted. The grounds are as follows:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">“Panchanani Shaha was not wife of Sharat Chandra Shaha and the plaintiff could not produce any evidence to prove that Panchanani Shaha was the wife of Sharat Chandra Shaha and as such, the plaintiff did not acquire any right, title and interest in the suit land but the High Court Division did not consider the aforesaid aspect and thus committed error of law resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The High Court Division failed to consider the evidence on record that the plaintiff hopelessly failed to prove their right, title and possession in the suit land. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The High Court Division failed to consider properly the meaning of gift under the Hindu Law and the law relating to the transfer of immovable property through gift.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The trial Court came to a finding that the plaintiffs could not prove that Panchanani was not a concubine of Sharat Chandra and that Dharijyamoyee having the life interest in half of ‘Kha’ schedule land did not have any right to transfer half of ‘Kha’ schedule land to Panchanani. The trial Court also found that the plaintiffs could not prove their title to and possession in the suit land. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The appellate Court on the other hand found that the ‘Ka’ schedule land and half of ‘Kha’ schedule land owned by Banomadhab Saha went to Tustalal Shaha, the sister’s son of Banomadhab Shaha and that the plaintiff are entitled to only half of the ‘Kha’ schedule land which Dharijyamoyee gifted to Panchanani by a registered deed of gift dated 07.10.1941. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The High Court Division found that the defendant has admitted in the written statement that the property was transferred to Panchanani Shaha by gift and that she remained in possession thereof on behalf of Tusta Lal. The High Court Division held that defendant-witnesses also admitted possession of Panchanani Shaha for some time. S.A. khatians which have been exhibited in Court and marked as exhibits-2(a)-2(f) show that the name of Panchanani had been recorded in the khatians and she paid rent regularly as shown by exhibit-5 series. The High Court Division further found that the alleged transfer of the suit land in favour of Panchanani by way of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘Youtuka’</em> and gift was acted upon. The High Court Division found that the plaintiffs’ contention to the effect that Tustalal died on 30.03.1964 before the death of Panchanani on 05.12.1967 was proved. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Admittedly, the ‘Ka’ schedule land belonged to Banomadhab Shaha and the ‘Kha’ schedule land belonged to Banomadhab Shaha and his nephew, Joytish Chandra Shaha in equal shares. The plaintiffs contended that Banomadhab Shaha having no son gifted his entire property as <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“Youtuka”</em> to his daughter Panchanani. The plaintiffs also contended that Joytish Chandra Shaha gifted his share orally to his mother Dharijyamoyee who gifted the same to his brother-in-law, Banomadhab’s daughter, Panchanani by a registered deed of gift dated 07.10.1941. Therefore, Panchanani became the owner of entire suit property. Panchanani died childless on 05.12.1964 (1374 B.S.). Her husband Sharat Chandra died on 16.03.1972 leaving behind three grandsons of his son, Purna Chandra who was the son of Sharat Chandra’s predeceased first wife Saralabala, that is, Purna Chanara was the step son of Panchanani. The names of the grandsons of Sarat Chandra Shaha are Prasenjit Saha, Nitaijit Shaha and Amarendra Nath Shaha alias Nirmaipada Shaha who are plaintiff Nos.1 to 3.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The defendant on the other hand contends that the suit property belonged to Banomadhab Shaha. Banomadhab Shaha died leaving behind daughter Panchanani and sister’s son Tustalal Shaha. According to the defendant as per Dayabaga succession, Panchani being a barren daughter of Banomadhab is excluded from inheriting the property left behind by Banomadhab and as such, Sharat Chandra Shaha, his grandsons, plaintiff Nos.1-3 were excluded from inheriting the property left behind by Banomadhab. The entire property has vested in the sister’s son Tutalal and thereafter upon Rashiklal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">It is to be seen whether Banomadhab could gift the ‘Ka’ schedule land and half of ‘Kha’ schedule to Panchanani by way of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘Youtuka’</em>. According to Dayabaga School, the plaintiffs as Panchanani’s step son’s sons stand at serial No.10 and in the absence of serial Nos.1-9, Panchanani’s son’s sons would inherit her <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘Youtuka’</em>. After the death of Panchanani’s husband Sharat Chandra, his grandsons inherited half of ‘Kha’ land from him. Admittedly, ‘<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Youtuka’</em> is a kind of gift and such gift if made at the time of marriage of daughter is valid in respect of immovable property and no registration is required according to section 123 of the Transfer of Property Act. <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘Youtuka’</em> has been defined in Molla’s Hindu Law twentieth edition <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘Youtuka’</em>, that is, gift made at the time of marriage. This term “Youtuka” has been interpreted by the High Court Division of Calcutta as including not only gifts made before the nuptial fire but gifts made during continuance of the marriage ceremonies, that is, the ceremonies beginning with shraddha and ending with that of prostrating before the husband. It is conceived that it includes gifts from strangers made before the nuptial fire and at the bridal procession.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In this connection reliance may be placed on the case of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Prem Mohan Das vs. Hari Mohan Das, ILR (1925) 52 Calcutta 425</em> where the plaintiff (father) had pronounced to give a house to his daughter and thus had induced the bridegroom’s party to agree to this marriage and he did not register the deed of gift but his daughter and son-in-law had been in possession of the said house for nearly 10 years in their own right. The father filed a suit to recover the house in question from the daughter’s transferee’s.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In the above case, it has been held that there was an ante-nuptial promise by the plaintiff which became a binding contract when the marriage followed and that the validity of such contract was well established.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In view of the above finding, we are of the view that <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘Youtuka’</em>, that is, gift of immovable property made as consideration of marriage at the time of nuptial fire is valid.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">       </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">As regards, the deeds of gift dated 07.10.1941 (exhibit-3), we find that in the said deed Panchanani was described as the wife of Sharat Chandra and as such, the claim of the defendants that Panchanani was concubine of Sharat Chandra has been falsified. Moreover, continuous living together for a long time proves that Sarat Chandra and Panchanani were husband and wife.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>In fact, Panchanani was the wife of Sharat Chandra and that she inherited ‘Ka’ schedule land and half of ‘Kha’ schedule land as ‘Youtuka’.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">It is contended that Dharijyamoyee had no right to make a deed of gift in favour of Panchanani and such gift was illegal and as such, half of ‘Kha’ schedule property did not pass to Panchanani. The appellate Court found that the deed of gift made by Dharijyamoyee in favour of Panchanani on 07.10.1941 was a valid document. The appellate Court found that even if it is found that Joytish Chandra did not make oral gift to Dharijyamoyee, Dharijyamoyee got half of ‘Kha’ schedule land after death of his son Joytish Chandra Shaha as life estate. The appellate Court rightly found that Dharijyamoyee could legally transfer the property which she got in life interest to Panchanani for legal necessity. The appellate Court noted that Dharijyamoyee became blind and Panchanani used to look after her and that prompted Dharijyamoyee to make gift of half of ‘Kha’ schedule land to Panchanani. Thereafter, Panchanani validly acquired half of ‘Kha’ schedule land by the deed of gift dated 07.10.1941. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Banomadhab’s sister’s son, Tustalal died on 30.03.1965 before Panchanani, who died on <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">05.12.1967. Therefore, Tustalal inherited nothing.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">As regards possession, the appellate Court found that the plaintiffs have been in possession in part of the suit land. The High Court Division, however, on consideration of the oral evidence and the S.A. khatians, exhibits-2(a)-2(f) and the rent receipts, exhibit-5 series found that the plaintiffs are in possession of the entire suit land. The finding of possession of the High Court Division having been based on proper appreciation of evidence on record does not call for interference. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In the light of the findings made before, we do not find any substance in these civil appeals. Accordingly, all the appeals are dismissed without any order as to costs.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">End of volume. </span></em></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue__June__18/Issue__June_18__C.%20A.%20225--330%20of%2009__Syed%20Mahmud%20Hossain,%20CJ___AD_2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">CIVIL APPEAL No. </span></u></strong></a><strong><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">325-330 of 2009.</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 9.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">(From the judgment and order dated 10.07.2008 passed by the High Court Division in <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Writ Petition Nos. 571-573 of 1987, 8692, 9205 and 9106 of 1991) </span></span></p></div></div></div></div>
632	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Masudur Rahman Vs.  Md. Shamsul Alam Hawlader and others, (Md. Nuruzzaman, J.)	 </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> First Appeal No. 236 of 2012 with Civil Rule No. 501(F) of 2012  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Nuruzzaman, J And S. H. Md. Nurul Huda Jaigirdar, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Swapan Kumar Dutta, Advocate ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2017</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Masudur Rahman @ Azahar Hossain  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Shamsul Alam Hawlader and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Evidence Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2019-12-02</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 150%; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: auto; border-collapse: collapse; margin-right: auto; height: 164px;" width="481"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 211.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Nuruzzaman, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt -5.4pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">And</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt 24.0pt -5.75pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">S. H. Md. Nurul Huda Jaigirdar, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">13.04.2017</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 36.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/article/18%20may%20aug/Issue__June__18/Issue%20__June__18__F.%20A.%20236%20of%2012_Md.%20Nuruzzaman,%20J.__2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p></td><td style="width: 189.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Masudur Rahman @ Azahar Hossain </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . . Appellant</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Shamsul Alam Hawlader and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .Respondents</span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">Evid</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">ence Act (I of 1872)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="color: #000000;">Sections 8 and 101</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">The man can tell a lie but facts, circumstances</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> and documents cannot. Moreso, only on the basis of oral evidence in the peculiar facts and circumstances of the case as has been discussed in the Judgment we are unable to belief the case of the plaintiff and decreed the suit in favor of him who by the materials on record has already proved that he is not real Masudur Rahman, rather, swindler Masudur Rahman who is admittedly Md. Azahar Hossain Bhuiyan of a clerk of the office of the Deputy Commissioner, Dhaka. It is the cardinal principles of the maxim of law of the land that the defects of the defendants cannot be the basis of the plaintiff rather, the plaintiff must prove his plaint case beyond the shadow of reasonable doubt. We find, therefore, that the judgment and decree passed by the trial Court neither </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.4pt;">beyond the documentary proofs nor committed</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> any error of law in flagrant violation of law. </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">The judgment and decree passed by the Court</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> below based upon the materials on record. In the above facts and circumstances and discussions made herein above we are of the </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">view that the impugned judgment and decree</span></strong> <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">does not call for any interference as the plaintiff</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> has failed to prove his case. . . .(102 to 104)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Erfan Ali Vs. Joynal Abedin, 35 DLR (AD) 216 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Swapan Kumar Dutta, Advocate </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the Appellant</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Mr. Abdul Halim Biswas Advocate with </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. M. Ataul Gani, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . . For the Respondents</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 27pt; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Nuruzzaman, J.</span></u></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The instant First Appeal at the instance of the plaintiff appellant is directed against the judgment and decree dated 22.5.2012 and 28.5.2012 respectively passed by the Joint District Judge, Additional Court, Dhaka in Title Suit No. 31 of 2012. (Originally Title Suit No. was 08 of 2002) dismissing the suit. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The material facts as have been derived from the plaint in short, are that the plaintiff instituted the suit for declaration of title over the suit property, recovery of Khas possession and cancellation of the deed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The plaintiff is the resident of village Perab, Police Station Sonargaon, District old Dhaka at present Narayangonj. The plaintiff’s name is Md. Azahar Hossain alias Masudur Rahman alias Masud Bhuyain. The father name of the plaintiff is Ahmed Hossain alias Shahjahan alias Shahjahan Bhuyain. The plaintiff while residing at Waisghat under Ward No. 06 of Kotwali Police Station purchased a shop in his wife’s name which is situated 95/C Elephant Road. The plaintiff’s wife has been doing business for long time. The marriage between the plaintiff and Most. Sabina Yeasmin was solemnized on 07.03.1980. In the Kabin nama, name of the plaintiff is Md. Azahar Hossain (Masud Bhuiyan) son of Ahmed Hossain (Shahjahan Bhuiyan). Mr. Razaul Karim the local member of Parliament issued a certificate on 9.1.2001 to the effect that the name of the plaintiff Md. Azahar Hossain alias Masudur Rahman son of Ahmed Hossain alias<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Shahjahan Bhuiyan. The plaintiff for long time was connected with the executive committee of a Mosque. On 2.9.2001 Mosque committee issued a certificate to the effect that the name of the plaintiff Md. Azahar Hossain alias Masud, son of Hazi Ahmed alias Shahjahan Bhuiyan. The plaintiff enlisted his name in the voter list. The plaintiff’s name in the voter list is Md.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Masudur Rahman (Azahar) son of Ahmed Hossain (Shahjahan), the plaintiff on 20.8.1989 made an affidavit being affidavit No. 203 before the Notary Public stating that the name of the plaintiff is Md. Azahar Hossain alias Masudur Rahman, son of Ahmed Hossain alias Shahjahan Bhuiyan. The plaintiff is an employee of the office of the Deputy Commissioner, Dhaka. The plaintiff’s father Md. Shahjahan Bhuiyan alias Ahmed Hossain Bhuiyan on 20.7.2002 made an affidavit before the learned Metropolitan Magistrate Mr. Biman Bhihari Bharua declaring that the plaintiffs name is Md. Azahar Hossain Bhuiyan alias Masudur Rahman.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">One Faizullah Bhuyan was the original owner of the suit property; the corresponding C.S. and S.A. Khatian also prepared accordingly in his name who thereafter vide a registered sale deed No. 5738 dated 11.10.1963 sold the same to one Nowab Ali Akond and made over its possession to the purchaser; Nowab Ali Akond also sold the same to one Helal Uddin Dhali and his wife Kanchan Nahar vide a registered sale deed No. 292 dated 27.01.1978. They also got their names mutated in the corresponding Khatian by filing a Mutation &amp; Jama Separation Case being No. 1211/1977-78. Thereafter for construction of building they also obtained an approved plan being No. 3906 dated 16.09.1978 from the DIT and constructed a building who thereafter vide a registered sale deed No.1558 dated 20.06.1991 sold the same to the plaintiff-appellant and made over its possession to him accordingly. After taking over possession as mentioned above the plaintiff-appellant engaged one Nazrul Islam Bhuyan as his caretaker to look after the property. He also rented the building to different monthly tenants through the said caretaker Nazrul Islam Bhuyan. He subsequently breached the trust of the plaintiff showing himself as Md. Masudur Rahman and started inducting monthly tenants by signing agreements behind the knowledge of the plaintiff. The plaintiff came to know the matter through the local terrorist and hooligan who themselves involved for grabbing the suit property. Nazrul Islam Bhuyan filed two police case being Nos. 35(3) 2000 and 39(3)2000 with Dhanmondi Police Station. The defendant Lutfar Rahman at this time came forward to take the possession of the property evicting the existing monthly tenants of the plaintiff-appellant through concocted and manufactured deed claiming that they purchased the land from one Masudur Rahman. Hence, Md. Yakub Ali, the Officer-in-Charge, Dhanmondi Police Station relying on the General Diary Entry No. 745 dated 13.03.2000 started a Non FIR Case being No. 102 of 2000 and also started a proceeding under section 145 of the Code of Criminal Procedure before the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate, Dhaka with a prayer for appointment of a receiver under section 146 of the Code of Criminal Procedure. The prosecution submitted a report suggesting the appointment of a receiver of the suit property Mr. Meraj Hossain, the learned Metropolitan Magistrate, Dhaka was pleased to attached the same on 17.03.2000 till further order. As this stage the plaintiff-appellant appeared with all supporting documents in that proceedings with a prayer for addition of party and for releasing the said property in his favour. Eventually, the matter was transferred to the Court of Mr. A.K.M. Abdus Salam who upon misconception of law and facts on 10.08.2001 directed to release the property in favour of the 2<sup>nd</sup> party. The plaintiff appellant against the said judgment and order 10.8.2001 filed a Criminal Revision being No. 344 of 2000 before the <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Sessions Judge, Dhaka. Eventually, the revision</span> was transferred to the Court of Additional Sessions Judge, 5<sup>th</sup> Court, who allowed the said Criminal revision and rescinded the order of appointment of receiver. The defendant-respondents also challenged the same order before the High Court Division of the Hon’ble Supreme Court of Bangladesh in Criminal Miscellaneous Case No. 5467 of 2001. The plaintiff-appellant also appeared in said case and contested in the said Criminal Miscellaneous Case but, unfortunately, when the matter was taken up for hearing the learned Advocate of his was not present before the Hon’ble High Court Division. Consequently, the Rule was made absolute on 13.02.2002 behind the knowledge of the plaintiff-appellant. The defendant-respondents as per the judgment and order of the High Court Division also took the possession of the suit property from the Officer-in-Charge, Dhanmondi Thana. Hence, the plaintiff filed the instant Suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The defendants Respondents Nos. 1-4 contested in the Suit by filing joint written statement. The defendants in their written statement denied the material allegations made in the plaint stating the different facts, inter alia, that:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The facts of the case of the answering defendants in short are that one <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Faizullah Bhuiyan</span> was the owner of the suit property. The said <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Faizullah Bhuiyan </span>on 11.10.1963 vide registered sale deed being deed No. 5738 sold the suit property to <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Nowab Ali Akhand. T</span>hereafter, said Nowab Ali Akhand got mutated the suit property on 17.10.1968 vide mutation Case being No. 771(1) PT/6768. Thereafter while said Nowab Ali had been owning and possessing the suit property for his personal necessity on 27.01.1978 sold the property vide registered sale deed being No. 292 to the Helal Uddin Dhali and his wife Khanchon Nahar. The Helal Uddin Dhali and his wife after purchasing the suit property filed a mutation case on 08.02.1978 and got mutated their name vide mutation Case being No. 1211(2) P-1/ 77-78. While Mr Helal Uddin Dhali and his wife had been owning and possessing the suit property without any disturbance and hindrance from any quarter they obtained and approved the plan being plan No. 3906 dated 16.09.1978 from the DIT now Rajuk. Mr. Dhali and his wife while had been owning and possessing the suit property sold the same vide a registered sale deed dated 20.06.1991 being sale deed No. 1558 to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Md. Masudur Rahman, son of Ahamed Hossain of 95/C, New Elephant Road, Dhanmondi, Dhaka and handed over the possession of the suit property to said Md. Masudur Rahman. The said Masudur Rahman got mutated his name vide Mutation Case being No. 2175(2)P-91 91-92 on<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>16.11.1992 and paid the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>rent. Mr. Masudur Rahman sold the suit property to the defendants on 17.4.2000 vide Registered sale deed being deed No. 1352 and handed over the possession of the property. The plaintiff to grab the suit property with building hatching conspiracy against the defendants with the connivance of Md. Yeakub Ali, the Officer in-charge of Dhanmondi Police Station. The Officer in-charge of Dhanmondi Police Station in the name of maintaining the peace started non FIR case being Dhanmondi Police Station case being No. 102 of 2000 and send a report to the Chief Metropolitan Magistrate for attachment of the suit property. The learned Chief Metropolitan Magistrate vide order No. 39 of 2000 attached the suit property and appointed the Officer in-charge as receiver of the suit property. Before the handover the possession of the suit property to the receiver on 13.3.2000 at midnight a daring dacoity had been committed while the defendants were in possession and living with family. The dacoits looted the ornaments, cash money, furniture with all documents of the defendants regarding the suit property. The police party at the time of occurrence of the dacoity was 20 yards distance from the suit house but they did not come forward to resist the dacoity rather, they helped the dacoits with a doubtful activities. The dacoity had been continuing about 2.00 P.M. to 5.00 P.M. Once again the defendants sought the assistance of Dhanmondi police but all are in vain.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The defendants on 13.3.2000 lodged a case with Dhanmondi Police Station and the same was registered as Dhanmondi P.S. Case No. 38 dated 13.3.2000. On 14.3.2000 the news of dacoity was published in the daily Ittefaq, the daily Janakantha, and the daily Inqilab. The Dhanmondi police did not publish or send any rejoinder regarding dacoity. So, it is proved that the Dhanmondi police tried to dispossess the defendants. However, the Dhanmondi police took the possession of the suit house by order of the learned Metropolitan Magistrate through Non-F.I.R. Case No. 102 of 2000. The defendant No. 4 Lutfar Rahman on 14.8.2000 lodged a case against the Caretaker of Nazrul Islam. The plaintiff and Md. Nazrul Islam in the Non F.I.R. case prayed for release and possession of the suit property in their favour. The learned Metropolitan Magistrate after hearing the matter opined that in the name of the so-called caretaker Md. Nazrul Islam made up a concocted case to grab the suit house. Hence, the applications for releasing and handing over the possession of the property in favour of them were rejected. The learned Magistrate further held that the applicant Md. Azharul Islam is not Masudur Rahman. Md. Azharul Islam is the employee of Deputy Commissioner Office. So, according to official service book the aforementioned order was passed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The defendants are the legal and lawful purchaser and owner of the suit property from the Masudur Rahman through registered sale deed and thereafter was on possession of the suit property until attachment by the Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The plaintiff as petitioner filed Criminal Revision being No. 344 of 2000 before the Metropolitan Sessions Judge against the order dated 10.8.2000 passed by the learned Metropolitan Magistrate. The aforesaid Criminal Revision was transferred to the Court of the Additional Sessions Judge, 5<sup>th</sup> Court, Dhaka who by the Judgment and Order dated 20.5.2001 allowed the Criminal Revision and thereby set aside the order dated 10.8.2000 passed by the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Metropolitan Magistrate. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The defendants being aggrieved by the order dated 20.5.2001 passed by the learned Additional Sessions Judge, 5<sup>th</sup> Court in Criminal Revision No. 344 of 2000 preferred the Criminal Miscellaneous case being No. 5467 of 2001.The Hon’ble Judges of the High Court Division heard the Rule on 13.2.2002 and by the Judgment and Order dated 20.05.2001 set aside the order of the learned<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Additional Sessions Judge, 5<sup>th</sup> Court, Dhaka, and cancelled the order of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the receiver. The Hon’ble High Court Division further directed the receiver to hand over the possession of the suit house to these defendants. Accordingly, the defendants are in possession of the suit property. In the above facts and circumstances they prayed for dismissal of the suit.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Joint District Judge, Additional Court, Dhaka upon perusing the averment of the plaint and written statement of the respective parties framed the following issues to determine the case:</span></p><ol start="1" style="margin-top: 0in; text-align: justify;" type="1"><li class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Is the case maintainable in its present form and manner?</span></li><li class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Is there any defect of parties in the suit?</span></li><li class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Is the plaintiff has any title over the suit property?</span></li><li class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Whether the plaintiff was dispossessed from the suit property?</span></li><li class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: justify; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Is the deed No.1352 dated 17.4.2000 fraudulent and voidable.</span></li></ol><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">At the trial the plaintiff’s side to prove the plaint case examined 3 P.Ws. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">P.W. 1. Md. Azaher Hosssain alias Masudur Rahman, P.W. 2-Md. Lutfor Rahman and P. W. 3 Md. Monirul Islam. The plaintiff side also produced some documents in the Court to prove his case which were marked as Exhibits. Affidavit dated 20.7.2002 Ext.-1, Original kabinnama, dated 7.3.1980 Ext.-2, Protoyan Potra (letter of authentication) dated 9.1.2001 ( with objection) Ext. 3,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>certified copy of the Mosque Committee Ext. 4, Voter list Ext. 5, affidavit dated 20.8. 1989, Ext. 6, S.A.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Khatian.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Ext. -7, Original deed being No. 5738<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>dated 11.10.1963 Ext. 8, certified copy of mutation<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>parcha being No. 180/1<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Ext. 9, original<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>deed being No. 292 dated 27.1.1978 Ext. 10, rent receipt (one page) Ext. 11, certified copy of lay out plan and clearance letter Ext. 12, certified copy of the original deed being No. 1558, dated 20.6.1991 Ext. 13, One rent receipt book Ext. 14, certified of the application dated 23.3.2000, Ext. 15, certified copy of the judgment of Criminal Revision being No. 344 of 2000 Ext. 16, certified copy of deed No. 1352 dated 17.4.2000 Ext. 17, National ID. Card Ext. 18, Passport Ext. 19, The Notice of Income Tax of four years Ext.-20, Income Tax return form with order for the year 2007-2008 Ext. 21.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">On the other hand, the defendants side to substantiate the defense case examined 5 D.Ws. D.W. No. 1 Shahjahan Howlader,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>D.W. No. 2 Md. Jalal. D.W. No. 3. Mortajur Rahman and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>D.W. No. 4<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Kazi Azizul Haque and D.W. No. 5 Reaz Ahmed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: HE;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The defendant side also produced some documents which were marked as Exts. Ext. ‘<strong>Ka</strong>’ certified copy of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>deed No. 5738, dated 11.10.1963, Ext. ‘<strong>Kha</strong>’ certified copy of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>deed No. 292 dated<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>27.1.1978, Ext. ‘<strong>ga’</strong> certified copy of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>deed No. 1558, dated 20.6.1991, Ext. <strong>‘Gha’</strong> certified copy of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>deed No. 1352, dated 17.4.2000 Ext. <strong>‘Uma-series’</strong> paper cutting<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of Daily Ittefaq, Daily Inquilab and Jano kantha, Ext. <strong>‘Cha’</strong> certified copy of judgment<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of the Metropolitan Magistrate passed in Non F.I.R. Case No. 102 of 2000, Ext. <strong>‘Chha’</strong> certified copy of order sheet of the Criminal Revision of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>5467 of 2001, Ext. <strong>‘S’</strong><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>certified copy of taking over the possession of the property,<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Ext. <strong>S</strong> -1, judgment of the High Court Division passed in Criminal Revision No. 5467 of 2001, Ext. <strong>‘T’,</strong> certified copy of the letter dated 13.7.2000, Ext. <strong>‘T</strong> -1’, certified copy of the letter dated 11.7.2000 Ext. <strong>‘U’- ‘U-1’</strong> certified copies of the order sheet of Misc. Case No. 36 of 2002 and Kanoongo report Ext. <strong>‘V’ </strong>certified copy of holding of tax and tax receipt. Exts. <strong>‘V’ series,</strong> copies of Dhaka Wasa and Sewerage bill, Ext. <strong>‘W’</strong> <strong>series,</strong> Electricity bill. Ext. <strong>‘X’</strong> <strong>series,</strong><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>copy of field Parcha of Khatian No. 2921, Ext. <strong>‘Y’,</strong> certified copy of Parcha of Khatian No. 1243 Ext. <strong>‘e’</strong> <strong>,</strong><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>letter of authentication of Income Tax, Ext. <strong>‘a’,</strong> Certified copies of Petition Case No. 221 of 2000 and Certified Copy of final report dated 31.12.2008 and Certified Copy of 164 of the Cr.Pc and order dated 27.05.2009 Ext. <strong>‘b’</strong> <strong>series, </strong>certified copy of the testimony of witness Monirul in the case of 102 of 2000 </span><span dir="RTL" lang="HE" style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Mangal',serif; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-language: HE;">‎</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-language: HE;">is Ext.</span><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> ‘c’</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-language: HE;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span>(with objection)</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 105%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 105%;">The learned Joint District Judge, additional Court, Dhaka upon considering the materials on record, after appreciating the testimonies of all the P.Ws. and D.Ws. and discussing the exhibits documents at the trial arrived at a decision that the plaintiff has failed to prove his case. Hence, by the judgment and decree dated 22.5.2012 and 28.5.2012 respectively dismissed the suit. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Being aggrieved by the impugned judgment</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> and decree dated 22.5.2012 and 28.5.2012 respectively the plaintiff as appellant preferred the instant first appeal before this Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Mr. Swapan Kumar Datta, the learned Advocate appearing for the appellant has submitted that the impugned judgment and decree dated 22.5.2012 passed by the learned Joint District Judge, Additional Court, Dhaka in Title Suit No. 31 of 2012 is bad in facts and <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">law and, as such, the same is liable to be set aside.</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">He has added that the trial Court upon misconception of law and evidences on record has failed to consider the settled principle of law and most illegally put the burden of proof upon the plaintiff without considering the settled proposition of law that if both the parties lead evidences to prove their respective cases then the onus of proof becomes academic and, as such, arrived at an illegal conclusion.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">According to Mr. Dutta, the trial Court misread and misunderstood the evidence of the contending parties specially the evidences of all the P.Ws. and D.Ws. though the P.Ws. are not only very much consistent to each other but also unequivocal and impartial in nature, but the trial Court most illegally disbelieved the same. On the other hand, though D.Ws. are inconsistent and equivocal in nature, but the trial Court most illegally relied on the same for the reason very much known to him.
