line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Yousuf Jamil Banu and others.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11pt; line-height: 110%;">General Clauses Act (X of 1897)</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="color: #000000;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Section 21</span></strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="color: #000000;">National Sports Council Act (XLVII of 1974)</span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Section 20A(a)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Under section 21 of the General Clauses Act while the power to add, to amend, vary or rescind notifications, orders, rules or bye-laws are available such power does not include the authority to take away validly acquired rights. Under section 21 of the General Clauses Act, the power conferred on NSC is not plenary power so as to make the power of BCB nugatory so far the amendment of the constitution is concerned unless such power is expressly conferred by the parent statute. The power conferred under Article 11.1 read with Article 26 of the Constitution is derived from the Act of 1974 and NSC had delegated the power to BCB to amend its constitution. By the memo dated 21.01.2012 NSC gave direction to BCB to include the proposed provisions in the Constitution of BCB and pursuant thereto BCB included those proposals of NSC and sent two copies of its constitutions to NSC for approval. NSC cannot do so in exercise of power under section 21 of the General Clauses Act ignoring the procedure for amendment of the constitution as contained in Articles 11.1 and 26. NSC, in fact, has usurped the power of BCB to amend its Constitution. Therefore, the High Court Division was justified in making the Rule absolute. Having considered all aspects of the case, we are of the view that the BCB is at liberty to amend its Constitution at any time as per provision of Article 11.1 and Article 26 of its Constitution so that the requirements of International Cricket Council is met subject to the approval of NSC.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">          </span><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">            </span>. . . (23 to 26)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(For the Appellant,</span></b><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>(In C. A. No.82/13)</span></b><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>) </span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, Senior Advocate (Mr. <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Shah Monjurul Hoque, Advocate</span> with him), instructed by Mrs. <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Madhumalati Chowdhury Barua,</span><span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> Advocate-on-Record. </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(For the Appellants,</span></b><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>(In C. A. No. 83/13)</span></b><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>) </span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;line-height:110%;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate (with Mr. Sheikh Fazle-Noor-Taposh, Advocate), instructed by Mvi. Md. Wahidullah, Advocate-on-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; text-indent: -0.5in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if supportFields]><b style='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><spanstyle='mso-element:field-begin'></span><spanstyle='mso-spacerun:yes'> </span>EQ \F(For the Respondents,</span></b><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:9.0pt;mso-bidi-font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>(In both the Appeals)</span></b><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'>) </span></b><![endif]--><!-- [if supportFields]><bstyle='mso-bidi-font-weight:normal'><span style='font-size:11.0pt;mso-bidi-font-family:"Courier New"'><span style='mso-element:field-end'></span></span></b><![endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">: </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. A. M. Aminuddin, Senior Advocate (Mr. Mahbub Shafiq, Advocate with him), instructed by Mrs. Shirin Afroz, Advocate-on-Record. </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 26pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; font-variant: small-caps;">Syed Mahmud Hossain, J</span></u></strong><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-fareast-font-family: BatangChe; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; font-variant: small-caps;">:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Both the appeals by leave are directed against the judgment and order dated 27.01.2013 passed by a Division Bench of the High Court Division in Writ Petition No. 16831 of 2012 making the Rule absolute.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The facts, relevant for the purpose of disposal of both the appeals, in a nutshell, are: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; text-indent: 26pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">On 23.01.2012, the Executive Committee of the Bangladesh Cricket Board (BCB) called an Extra-Ordinary General Meeting (EGM) on 1<sup>st</sup> March, 2012 for considering amendment of its constitution. In the said EGM, the members present approved the amendment of the constitution of BCB. Accordingly as per provisions of Article 11.1 of the Articles of Association, the BCB by letter dated 28<sup>th</sup> August, 2012 sent the proposed amendment to the National Sports Council (NSC) and sought final approval. The NSC upon detailed study of the proposed amendment, by the letter dated 21<sup>st</sup> October, 2012 and 22<sup>nd</sup> November, 2012 incorporated certain amendments to the proposed constitution of BCB and directed BCB to include the said amendments in its constitution and thereafter, to forward two copies of the amended constitution to the NSC for approval. As per direction of the NSC, BCB inserted the said amendment in its constitution and forwarded the same to NSC. Thereafter, NSC by Memo No. </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">GbGm/wm/120/3/‡Rm/3324</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> dated 29<sup>th</sup> November, 2012 approved the <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">proposed amendment to the constitution of BCB.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Challenging the impugned amendment and the final approval of the Constitution <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(</span></span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">NWea¿»)</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;"> of the BCB so made by writ-respondent</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> No.4 vide memo No. </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">GbGm/wm/120/3/‡Rm/3324</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> dated 29.11.2012 (Annexure-H), the writ-petitioners filed an application under Article 102 of the Constitution of Bangladesh and obtained Rule Nisi in Writ Petition No. 16831 of 2012.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Writ-respondent Nos.3 and 5 contested the Rule by filing an affidavit-in-opposition controverting the material statements made in the writ-petition. Their case, in short, is that the BCB being an affiliated body of the NSC, NSC is legally authorized under section 20A(a) of the National Sports Council Act, 1974 (in short, Act of 1974) to frame “model constitution” for all or any of the organizations affiliated to it. It has further been stated that in compliance with the provision of Article 26 of the constitution of BCB, the impugned amendment has been made and as such, allegation of non-compliance with the aforesaid provision does not arise at all. It has also been stated that the amended constitution has been made as per instructions and standard model of the International Cricket Council and that the present ad-hoc committee of BCB is discharging its functions accordingly as per amended Constitution of the BCB. In other words, the said impugned amendment has already been acted upon. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The learned Judges of the High Court Division upon hearing the parties by the judgment and order dated 27.01.2013 made the Rule absolute and declared the impugned amendment of BCB approved by Annexure-H to have been made without lawful authority.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">   </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Feeling aggrieved by and dissatisfied with impugned judgment and order passed by the High Court Division, writ-respondent Nos.5, Secretary, NSC as the leave-petitioner filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.573 of 2013 and writ-respondent No.6, BCB<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>and another filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No.431 of 2013 before this Division and obtained leave in both the civil petitions on 25.07.2013, resulting in Civil Appeal No.82 and 83 of 2013. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Mahbubey Alam, learned Senior Advocate, appearing on behalf of the appellant (NSC) of Civil Appeal Nos.82 of 2013, submits that BCB is an affiliated body of NSC and as per provision of section 20A(a) of the Act of 1974, the authority can frame model constitution for all or any of the organizations affiliated to it and as such there is no illegality in amending the constitution of the BCB but the High Court Division without considering the same made the Rule absolute and as such, the impugned judgment should be set aside. He further submits that the High Court Division failed to appreciate that a mere Article of the Articles of the Association of BCB, namely, Article 26 cannot curtail the power of National Sports Council (NSC) under the Act of 1974 and as such, the impugned judgment is not sustainable in law. He then submits that the High Court Division erred in law in failing to appreciate that section 20A(a) of the Act of 1974 read with section 21 of the General Clauses Act and Article 11(1) of the Constitution of BCB has empowered the NSC to frame and also amend the constitution of BCB and as such the impugned judgment is not sustainable in law. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. Rokanuddin Mahmud, learned Senior Advocate, appearing on behalf of the appellant (BCB) of Civil Appeal No.83 of 2013, submits that the amendment of the constitution has been <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">made as per instruction of the NSC and the present</span> ad-hoc committee of BCB is discharging its function as per amended constitution of BCB. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Mr. A.M. Aminuddin, learned Senior Advocate, appearing on behalf of the writ-petitioner-respondents of both the appeals, supports the impugned judgment delivered by the High Court Division. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">We have considered the submissions of the learned Senior Advocates of both the sides, perused the impugned judgment and the materials on record. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">NSC is an autonomous body constituted under National Sports Council Act, 1974 (Act No. XLVII of 1974) (in short, the Act of 1974). The Bangladesh Cricket Board (in short, the <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">BCB) is a recognized national sports organization</span> and an affiliated body of the NSC having its own Constitution under the name and style “</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">h¡wm¡­cn ¢H²­LV ®h¡XÑ NWea¿» (2008 pe fkÑ¿¹ pw­n¡¢da)</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">” (Annexure-A) being approved by NSC. According to Article 11.1 of the Constitution, BCB has the authority to amend its constitution subject to the approval of NSC. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Article 26 of the constitution of BCB prescribed the procedures for amendment of its constitution. Article 26 runs as under: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 32.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">“</span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">According to the aforesaid provision, the Executive Committee of BCB convened several meetings and ultimately at its 34<sup>th</sup> Extra-Ordinary General Meeting held on 01.03.2012, the proposed amendment (Annexure-C-1) had been adopted and ultimately, it was forwarded to the Secretary, NSC for final approval. The contents of the office letter dated 21.10.2012 (Annexure-E) is quoted below: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 26pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">mwPe</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 1in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: SutonnyBanglaMJ; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">RvZxq µxov cwil`</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Now it is to be resolved whether NSC can amend the Constitution of the BCB of its <span style="letter-spacing: -.5pt;">own accord without the amendment being approved</span> by BCB as per Article 26 of the Constitution. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Section 10 of the Act of 1974 deals with the function of NSC constituted under section 3(1) of the Act of 1974. Clause (b) of section 10 of the Act of 1974 provides that NSC shall have the power to grant recognition and the affiliation to the sports organizations. Section <span style="letter-spacing: -.4pt;">12(2)(f) of the Act of 1974 provides that the Executive Committee of NSC shall have the power to issue such directives as it may deem necessary in the interest of promotion of the sports.</span> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Section 20A of the Act of 1974, in particular, in clause (a) provides that NSC shall have power to frame model constitution for all or any of the organizations so affiliated to it. The relevant provision of section 20A of the Act of 1974 is quoted below: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 26pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">   </span>“20A. Notwithstanding anything contained in any other law for the time being in force, or in any agreement, contract, memorandum or articles of association or any other legal instrument, the Council shall have power-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 45.5pt; text-indent: -19.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">to frame model constitution for all or <span style="letter-spacing: -.2pt;">any of the organisations affiliated to it;</span><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 45.5pt; text-indent: -19.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">....................................</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 45.5pt; text-indent: -19.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">....................................</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 45.5pt; text-indent: -19.5pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">...................................</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12pt; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>As regards the amendment of the Constitution, BCB has its authority to do so as per Article 26 of the Constitution as stated earlier.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">In this connection, it is to be mentioned here that Article 11 of the Constitution of BCB provides the power of General Body </span><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">(p¡d¡le f¢loc)z</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"> Article 11.1 states as under: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">""Ae¤­µRc-11 x p¡d¡lZ f¢lo­cl c¡¢uaÄx</span></u></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>p¡d¡lZ f¢lo­cl c¡¢uaÄ J L¡kÑf¢l¢d ¢ejÀl²f qC­hx</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">11|1 ¢h¢p¢hl NWea¿» fËZue J fË­u¡S­e pw­n¡dez k¡q¡ flha£Ñ­a S¡a£u H²£s¡ f¢loc La«ÑL Ae¤­j¡¢ca qC­a qC­hz</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">11.2 ------------------------------------------------</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 0.25in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">11.3-----------------------------------------------''</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">There is no gainsaying the fact that NSC is the controlling authority of all sports organizations of the country including BCB. As per section 20A of the Act of 1974, the NSC has framed the Constitution of BCB or has approved the constitution as framed by BCB.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">According to Article 11.1 read with Article 26 of the Constitution of BCB, the power to amend the constitution has been given to BCB subject to the approval of NSC. By section 20A of the Act of 1974, the legislator has given the power to NSC to frame constitution and pursuant to that power the constitution has been duly framed and NSC by doing so delegated the power of amendment of the Constitution to BCB with its approval. Record reveals that BCB in exercise of the power of amendment has effected amendments to its constitution on previous occasions with the approval of NSC. Pursuant to the provisions of Articles 11.1 and 26 of the constitution, a right has accrued to BCB to amend its constitution which cannot be curtailed by NSC. It is of course correct that NSC has the power to accord approval to any amendment to the constitution of BCB but NSC cannot impose any amendment on BCB. If such a practice is allowed then the provisions of Articles 11.1 and 26 of the Constitution of BCB will become <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">meaningless. Moreover, BCB should be allowed</span> to work freely in respect of amendments of its constitution without any direct interference by NSC which, of course, has the power to accord approval to such amendment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 6pt; text-indent: 0in; text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">It is contended that section 20A(a) of the Act of 1974 read with section 21 of the General Clauses Act, 1897 authorities NSC to amend the Constitution of BCB. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6pt; text-indent: 26pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Section 21 of the General Clauses Act, 1897 provides as under:<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 26pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">“Power to make to include power to add to, amend, vary or rescind, orders, rules or bye-laws-</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Where, by any Act of Parliament or Regulation, a power to issue notifications, orders, rules, or bye-laws is conferred, then that power includes a power, exercisable in the like manner and subject to the like sanction and conditions (if any), to add to, amend, vary or rescind any notifications, orders, rules or bye-laws so issued.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 26.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">23.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Under section 21 while the power to add, to amend, vary or rescind notifications, orders, rules or bye-laws are available such power does not include the authority to take away validly acquired rights. Under section 21 of the General Clauses Act, the power conferred on NSC is not plenary power so as to make the power of BCB nugatory so far the amendment of the constitution is concerned unless such power is expressly conferred by the parent statute.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 26.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">24.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">The power conferred under Article 11.1 read with Article 26 of the Constitution is derived from the Act of 1974 and NSC had delegated the power to BCB to amend its constitution. By the memo dated 21.01.2012 (Annexure-E) NSC gave direction to BCB to include the proposed provisions in the Constitution of BCB and pursuant thereto BCB included those proposals of NSC and sent two copies of its constitutions to NSC for approval. NSC cannot do so in exercise of power under section 21 of the General Clauses Act ignoring the procedure for amendment of the constitution as contained in Articles 11.1 and 26. NSC, in fact, has usurped the power of BCB to amend its Constitution. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 26.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">25.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Therefore, the High Court Division was justified in making the Rule absolute. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 26.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">26.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">Having considered all aspects of the case, we are of the view that the BCB is at liberty to amend its Constitution at any time as per provision of Article 11.1 and Article 26 of its Constitution so that the requirements of International Cricket Council is met subject to the approval of NSC. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level5 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt .5in; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .25in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Calibri',sans-serif; mso-fareast-font-family: Calibri; mso-bidi-font-family: Calibri; mso-ansi-language: EN;">1)</span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New';">   Accordingly, both the appeals are disposed of with the observations made in the body of the judgment.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin: 0in 0in 12pt 26pt; text-align: justify;"> </p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="text-align: justify;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p style="margin: 0in; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(From the judgment and order dated 27.01.2013 passed by the High Court Division in <span style="mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">Writ Petition No. 16831 of 2012) </span></span></p></div></div></div></div>
